  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

<span id="freeTextContainer4643956364656486618">The year is 1984 and the city is Tokyo.<br/><br/>A young woman named Aomame follows a taxi driver’s enigmatic suggestion and begins to notice puzzling discrepancies in the world around her. She has entered, she realizes, a parallel existence, which she calls 1Q84 —“Q is for ‘question mark.’ A world that bears a question.” Meanwhile, an aspiring writer named Tengo takes on a suspect </span>
  <span id="freeText4643956364656486618" style="display:none">The year is 1984 and the city is Tokyo.<br /><br />A young woman named Aomame follows a taxi driver’s enigmatic suggestion and begins to notice puzzling discrepancies in the world around her. She has entered, she realizes, a parallel existence, which she calls 1Q84 —“Q is for ‘question mark.’ A world that bears a question.” Meanwhile, an aspiring writer named Tengo takes on a suspect ghostwriting project. He becomes so wrapped up with the work and its unusual author that, soon, his previously placid life begins to come unraveled. <br /><br />A love story, a mystery, a fantasy, a novel of self-discovery, a dystopia to rival George Orwell’s—1Q84 is Haruki Murakami’s most ambitious undertaking yet: an instant best seller in his native Japan, and a tremendous feat of imagination from one of our most revered contemporary writers</span>
  <a data-text-id="4643956364656486618" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Yes, there are three "books" and this one contains only the first two. In Japan, the two first books were published in 2009 on the same date while the<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Yes, there are three "books" and this one contains only the first two. In Japan, the two first books were published in 2009 on the same date while the third book was published in 2010. Vintage has decided to publish them in the same constellation.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/14114603-elleh-rachelle"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1351664562i/14114603._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">If I were you I wouldn't think of skipping any pages, there is no repeats however the chapters are linked according to the three characters Aomame, Te<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">If I were you I wouldn't think of skipping any pages, there is no repeats however the chapters are linked according to the three characters Aomame, Tengo and Ushikawa. So if you skip the pages or chapters, you might not get the actual story, however there are something that you can ignore like the parts or sections where the author has borrowed stories from others work, of course giving full credit. <br />This book is my best read I can say this year, unless another book wins me.☺☺☺<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_245753429" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/245753429" />
    <a title="Shauna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6394569-shauna"><img alt="Shauna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372774005p2/6394569.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/245753429?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shauna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shauna" href="/user/show/6394569-shauna">Shauna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Lovers of the female form</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6394569-shauna?shelf=japan-manga">japan-manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6394569-shauna?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer245753429" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3404360002272468842">1Q84 is not a good book. At all.<br/><br/>I cannot understand the hype surrounding this book. The storyline wasn't bad in itself but…1Q84 reads like the fantasy of a sad, balding (you'll understand) ageing man. <br/><br/>Leaving to one side Murakami's breast obsession-and, in fact, I don't think there's a single female character who's breasts I couldn't give you a detailed account of-it was the author's handling of female characters that truly bothered me. <br/>Aomame, the female protagonist, an assassin who in her free</span>
  <span id="freeText3404360002272468842" style="display:none">1Q84 is not a good book. At all.<br /><br />I cannot understand the hype surrounding this book. The storyline wasn't bad in itself but…1Q84 reads like the fantasy of a sad, balding (you'll understand) ageing man. <br /><br />Leaving to one side Murakami's breast obsession-and, in fact, I don't think there's a single female character who's breasts I couldn't give you a detailed account of-it was the author's handling of female characters that truly bothered me. <br />Aomame, the female protagonist, an assassin who in her free time prowls around looking for men to have casual sex with. Not just any men though;<br /><i>Aomame herself did not know why, but ever since the time she was twenty, she had been attracted to men with thinning hair.</i><br />Right.<br />Do you get the balding thing now? Or, even more revealing;<br /><i>She was dying to run her fingers through the few strands he had left</i><br />Yes Murakami, yes. That is absolutely and 100% realistic, don't let a bit of thinning hair get you down.<br /><br />That in itself though, fine. It takes all kinds, and Murakami's little fantasy woman is more humorous than anything. He could have being trying for humor-and the book did have me laughing for the first few chapters-but the more the book progressed, the more objectionable the author's portrayal of women became until it really, really bothered me. <br />By the end of book one, no curiosity about the 'Little People' or interest in seeing the actual coming together of Tengo and Aomame could compell me to stiff-upper-lip my way through another volume.<br /><br />To be fair, much of what bothered me with this book could be to a simple clashing of cultures. Not even getting into how wrong I found Murakami's handling of the female characters; the male protagonist Tengo was ruined for me when it became clear he was running with his interest in the 17 year-old Fuka-Eri. <br />No matter how much you dig her breasts Tengo-and really, he creates near odes to them in his head- Fuka-Eri is a traumatized, mentally fragile near-mute with the mind of a child. Not o.k. Tengo, not o.k.<br />But then, I have read that the age of consent in Japan is what I would consider alarmingly low.<br /><br />Murakami, you like breasts and you like to imagine in women a certain way.. fair play to you-we all have our little quirks and you'd be among many-but keep it inside next time. Please.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3404360002272468842" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_217888824" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/217888824" />
    <a title="Sam Still Reading" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/162915-sam-still-reading"><img alt="Sam Still Reading" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1232938717p2/162915.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/217888824?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam Still Reading" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam Still Reading" href="/user/show/162915-sam-still-reading">Sam Still Reading</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Sam Still Reading by: </span>
      ARC copy
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer217888824" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8204745720461883421">I finished reading 1Q84 (surely the blockbuster novel of 2011) almost a week ago, but I wanted to collect my thoughts before I put fingers to keyboard. This is a novel (sounds trite, perhaps epic would be a better word) that remains with you for a long, long time after reading it. I’ve kept thinking about the story and how each event fits in the overall structure of the book, how clever and intricate the world created is and how I can picture in my head a world that doesn’t exist…or does it?<br/><br/>The </span>
  <span id="freeText8204745720461883421" style="display:none">I finished reading 1Q84 (surely the blockbuster novel of 2011) almost a week ago, but I wanted to collect my thoughts before I put fingers to keyboard. This is a novel (sounds trite, perhaps epic would be a better word) that remains with you for a long, long time after reading it. I’ve kept thinking about the story and how each event fits in the overall structure of the book, how clever and intricate the world created is and how I can picture in my head a world that doesn’t exist…or does it?<br /><br />The ARC copy I read comprised of Books 1 and 2 (Book 3 will be published in the UK on 25th October 2011, I’m uncertain of an Australian release date). The sheer weight of the first two books (nearly 600 pages) will come as a delight to Murakami fans. For readers new to Murakami, it may take a little while to warm up to the picture that is being painted lovingly before you but persevere, the puzzle pieces soon fall into place. The book opens with Aomame (whose name means ‘green pea’, we never know her by any other name) in a taxi, stuck in a traffic jam in Tokyo in 1984. She is going to be late for her appointment when the taxi driver informs her of an emergency exit that will take her off the expressway back to ground level. He says a few odd things, but Aomame is not concerned about that. She takes his advice, goes down the stairs and off to her appointment – killing a man.<br /><br />Meanwhile, Tengo is a young writer who is struggling to make a name for himself while teaching mathematics at a cram school. At a meeting with his somewhat mentor, he is asked to rewrite a novel written by a seventeen year old girl that has been submitted for a new writers’ prize. The novel, Air Chrysalis, is nothing like he’s ever read before. Neither is its author, Fuka-Eri, a strange girl who never uses a question mark in her speech.<br /><br />Can you see the Murakami originality coming through? The cover pictured gives quite an insight into the main symbols of this book.<br /><br />I don’t want to spoil the story for others – it’s highly original and will keep you reading all through the night but be prepared for almost anything to happen: religious cults, strange sightings of the moon, an older woman out for revenge, missing persons, murder, love, sex and all sorts of people – from big to small.<br /><br />Murakami must be lauded for his ability to think of such an intricate plot – almost every detail is leading you further into the story and almost nothing is there by chance. It all combines together later in the second book with exquisite tension before the explosion of the bittersweet ending. Be aware that there is a fair bit of sex in this book but I felt it was needed to show where the characters were coming from and where they were heading. <br /><br />On finishing this book, I hardly dared to look up at the moon in case I was in 1Q84! Everything else I’ve read since has paled in comparison to 1Q84. I simply can’t recommend this book more highly – it’s a beautiful masterpiece. <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://samstillreading.wordpress.com">http://samstillreading.wordpress.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8204745720461883421" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_411842896" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/411842896" />
    <a title="Toby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5454475-toby"><img alt="Toby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542247337p2/5454475.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/411842896?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Toby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Toby" href="/user/show/5454475-toby">Toby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099549062" href="/book/show/15822556-1q84">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5454475-toby?shelf=fantastical">fantastical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5454475-toby?shelf=translation">translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5454475-toby?shelf=lit">lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer411842896" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11465240158530914665"><b>“If you can't understand it without an explanation, you can't understand it with an explanation.”</b><br/><br/>An oft repeated phrase throughout the first two books of what has been described as Haruki Murakami's magnum opus by an overly enthusiastic reviewer desperate to get a quote on the cover of the book, and one that obviously works as a message to the reader confused by the lack of explanation for events throughout the novel.<br/><br/>Being only two thirds through the novel at this stage I cannot provide a full r</span>
  <span id="freeText11465240158530914665" style="display:none"><b>“If you can't understand it without an explanation, you can't understand it with an explanation.”</b><br /><br />An oft repeated phrase throughout the first two books of what has been described as Haruki Murakami's magnum opus by an overly enthusiastic reviewer desperate to get a quote on the cover of the book, and one that obviously works as a message to the reader confused by the lack of explanation for events throughout the novel.<br /><br />Being only two thirds through the novel at this stage I cannot provide a full response to the text, I would have preferred to buy each book individually for psychological reasons more than anything, the size of this novel is intimidating, but this is the year of reading big books and so I finally built up the courage to tackle 805 pages and such is the casual and playful nature of Murakami's prose in this instance that I hardly noticed how heavy the book itself was.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Things like this don't happen all that often in one lifetime. This is the magnificent world of a picaresque novel. Just brace yourself and enjoy the smell of evil. We're shooting the rapids. And when we go over the falls, let's do it together in grand style!”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Murakami is constantly drawing attention to the tools of a writer, the act of reading and the conventions of both but not in the obnoxious way that it seems most contemporary literary sensations seem to revel in. His passion for his chosen profession is what shines through the most, his adoration for Dickens, Orwell, Chekov etc rather than a simple and gratuitous aping of what has come before.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>"I am nothing. I’m like someone who’s been thrown into the ocean at night, floating all alone. I reach out, but no one is there. I call out, but no one answers. I have no connection to anything.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />On face value 1Q84 is an exact replica of his other works and at the same time nothing at all like what has come before. He touches on the same themes, in true Quentin Tarantino fashion his sexual fetish is made obvious, the bleeding together of reality and fantasy, the dislocated lives of his protagonists but most prominent is the fact that this is his most romantic work since Norwegian Wood, that special kind of magical and tortured romance you seem to only find in the novels of Haruki Murakami.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Wasn't it better if they kept this desire to see each other hidden within them, and never actually got together? That way, there would always be hope in their hearts. That hope would be a small, yet vital flame that warmed them to their core-- a tiny flame to cup one's hands around and protect from the wind, a flame that the violent winds of reality might easily extinguish.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />A lot has been made of the length (massive) and the fact that there's so much repetition of basic information but beyond some mild irritation I can't say I really noticed. I frequently realised that I was X number of pages in and not much had actually happened, plot development was minimal or the direction was vague but these are not bad things when part of a story told by Haruki Murakami, especially one told in such vivid detail. <br /><br />I'm very much looking forward to finding out if anything gets resolved, if anything starts to make any sense at all, if the star crossed lovers find happiness, what exactly it is that the Little People have planned and the answers to any number of other fascinating and intriguing questions that have been posed throughout, but then if the general theme so far is anything to go by perhaps I will be pondering the meaning for many years to come.<br /><br /><b>“It is not that the meaning cannot be explained. But there are certain meanings that are lost forever the moment they are explained in words.”</b><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/411842893" rel="nofollow noopener">Book 3 Review</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11465240158530914665" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_210833880" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/210833880" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/166366-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577986999p2/166366.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/210833880?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/166366-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer210833880" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10863569600568614140">I'm sad to report that I didn't so much love this book. I didn't hate it but felt gypped a bit, and I guess that comes from all the hoop-la. I am however proud that I can now boast that I can read a 900 page book. This also means I don't have an excuse not to finish up Ulysses. Nuts. Anywhoooo, I'm going to be direct and list what I didn't love:<br/><br/>1. TOO LONG. This might be a given, but after finishing all 900 pages I can safely say that he could have cut it by half. Did anything even happen in the</span>
  <span id="freeText10863569600568614140" style="display:none">I'm sad to report that I didn't so much love this book. I didn't hate it but felt gypped a bit, and I guess that comes from all the hoop-la. I am however proud that I can now boast that I can read a 900 page book. This also means I don't have an excuse not to finish up Ulysses. Nuts. Anywhoooo, I'm going to be direct and list what I didn't love:<br /><br />1. TOO LONG. This might be a given, but after finishing all 900 pages I can safely say that he could have cut it by half. Did anything even happen in the last third of the book? Not so much.<br /><br />2. Lame ending. I'm not going to spoil anything, but after slogging through 900 pages you expect some fireworks at the end. One measly fire cracker even? Not so much.<br /><br />3. Clunky and wooden language which made for clunky and wooden characters. Was it just me or did these seem like Japanese robots versus people? I always thought his translators did a brilliant job but I think they missed the mark on this one. Maybe the switch from first to third person narrative? <br /><br />4. The Murakami obesssions started to get to me. I know he's obsessed with cats, lesbian love scenes, and the magic of pubic hair, but it started to get a little overboard. At times the whole book felt like a wet dream of prepubescent boy. <br /><br />I didn't hate the book, but don't think it at all lives up to his earlier stuff. There were certainly moments of brilliance, but I would not necessarily recommend it to anyone. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10863569600568614140" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2603018397" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2603018397" />
    <a title="Cynnamon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/73483095-cynnamon"><img alt="Cynnamon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541975560p2/73483095.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2603018397?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cynnamon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cynnamon" href="/user/show/73483095-cynnamon">Cynnamon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9783442743629" href="/book/show/16003811-1q84">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73483095-cynnamon?shelf=kat-scifi">kat-scifi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2603018397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11550487845629300035">For a long time I was a bit afraid to read this book. Everything I had heard about it made me suspect that it was very challenging to read in both style and content. <br/><br/>What a surprise when I finally got started. <br/><br/>The writing style is extremely clear and pleasant and the content really got me carried away. <br/><br/>It's about Aomame and Tengo, who once had contact in their childhood. They're around thirty now and haven't seen each other in 20 years. I think Aomame is the more interesting character. In my opi</span>
  <span id="freeText11550487845629300035" style="display:none">For a long time I was a bit afraid to read this book. Everything I had heard about it made me suspect that it was very challenging to read in both style and content. <br /><br />What a surprise when I finally got started. <br /><br />The writing style is extremely clear and pleasant and the content really got me carried away. <br /><br />It's about Aomame and Tengo, who once had contact in their childhood. They're around thirty now and haven't seen each other in 20 years. I think Aomame is the more interesting character. In my opinion, Tengo is a bit of a sluggish bore, but despite his passivity he contributes to the progress of the story. <br /><br />The story is told from the point of view of these two protagonists and contains a number of fantastic elements. <br /><br />I can't say more about the content at the moment, because on the one hand I want to avoid spoilers and on the other hand a lot is still unclear. <br /><br />This book ends with a cliffhanger, which is not surprising as it only contains the first two parts of a trilogy. <br /><br />I found this novel mesmerizing and I will definitely read the third volume too. <br /><br />I rate with 4.5 stars, which I round up to 5. <br /><br /> ---------------------------------------<br /> <br /><br />An dieses Buch habe ich mich sehr lange nicht herangetraut. Alles, was ich darüber gehört hatte, ließ mich vermuten, dass es sowohl vom Stil als auch vom Inhalt sehr anspruchsvoll zu lesen sei. <br /><br />Was für eine Überraschung als ich endlich damit begonnen habe. <br /><br />Der Schreibstil ist äußerst klar und angenehm und der Inhalt hat mich wirklich mitgerissen. <br /><br />Es geht um Aomame und Tengo, die in ihrer Kindheit mal Kontakt hatten. Jetzt sind sie um die Dreißig und haben sich seit 20 Jahren nicht gesehen. Aomame halte ich für den interessanteren Charakter. Tengo ist in meinen Augen eher eine träge Dumpfbacke, der aber trotz seiner Passivität zum Fortschreiten der Story beiträgt. <br /><br />Die Geschichte wird wechselseitig aus der Sicht dieser beiden Protagonisten erzählt und enthält etliche fantastische Elemente. <br /><br />Zum Inhalt kann ich derzeit nicht mehr sagen, da ich zum einen nicht spoilern möchte und zum anderen vieles noch unklar geblieben ist. <br /><br />Dieses Buch endet mit einem Cliffhanger, was nicht weiter verwunderlich ist, da es nur die ersten beiden Teile einer Trilogie enthält. <br /><br />Mich hat der Roman richtiggehend in seinen Bann gezogen und ich werde den dritten Band auf jeden Fall auch lesen. <br /><br />Bewerten möchte ich mit 4,5 Sternen, die ich auf 5 aufrunde. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11550487845629300035" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_304549339" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/304549339" />
    <a title="Virginia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7325637-virginia"><img alt="Virginia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329408257p2/7325637.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/304549339?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia" href="/user/show/7325637-virginia">Virginia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer304549339" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16451808271286527305">I've been on the Murakami bandwagon since a friend introduced me to the Wind-Up Bird, but I am now officially getting off.<br/><br/>The core idea has so much potential, but it drowns - screaming - in a sea of inept, boring, repetitive language. I was literally scratching my head wondering how this book escaped a ruthless editing. There is no justification - other than author laziness and/or vanity - for this book to be so damn long. I was so surprised at the mediocrity of the prose that I kept wondering w</span>
  <span id="freeText16451808271286527305" style="display:none">I've been on the Murakami bandwagon since a friend introduced me to the Wind-Up Bird, but I am now officially getting off.<br /><br />The core idea has so much potential, but it drowns - screaming - in a sea of inept, boring, repetitive language. I was literally scratching my head wondering how this book escaped a ruthless editing. There is no justification - other than author laziness and/or vanity - for this book to be so damn long. I was so surprised at the mediocrity of the prose that I kept wondering whether the issue was in the translation.<br /><br />Mr Murakami I have come up with some quick and easy suggestions to reduce word count<br /><br />I gather you're a breast man and other reviewers have noted that every female character is described with reference to her breast shape and size. This rapidly becomes tiring, but as a writer it is inexcusable that you continually have your lead female character contemplate the size of her breasts, in much the same way and to no additional significance than the first time she does so. Move the fuck on. DELETE UNNECESSARY BREAST CONTEMPLATION - 400 WORDS SAVED<br /><br />So much of your dialogue is characters simply repeating the last thing they heard. Such a clumsy way to indicate confusion (if that's what you're trying to do). And all of them, the same device? No way. DELETE REPEATED DIALOGUE - 500 WORDS SAVED<br /><br />You introduce us to the idea very early on that Fuka-Eri has unusual uninflected speech. I do not need you to repeat at every utterance "She asked with no question mark". DELETE "with no question mark" and all of Tengo's comments that she asks questions with no question mark. 600 WORDS SAVED.<br /><br />I could go on, but I've wasted so much time reading this book that I draw the line at wasting more on it here. I'll just say that I was saddened to read the clumsy way Murakami manipulated characters and setting to maintain ambiguity for it's own sake. <br /><br />I love ambiguity, I love complexity and I am always willing to suspend disbelief. I just prefer it to be well-written. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16451808271286527305" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16258742611990950701">I can't really give this book a proper review seeing as I've only completed 2/3s of it so far - but I FEEL like I've climbed a mountain these past 3 weeks! Murakami's prose is spot on as usual, and the story itself is completely bizarre and intriguing - probably the most heavy magical realism I've read from him so far. I really enjoy the dual perspective, but I still have so many questions. I doubt (from what I've heard) that they'll be cleared up in the third volume but I'm still intrigued to r</span>
  <span id="freeText16258742611990950701" style="display:none">I can't really give this book a proper review seeing as I've only completed 2/3s of it so far - but I FEEL like I've climbed a mountain these past 3 weeks! Murakami's prose is spot on as usual, and the story itself is completely bizarre and intriguing - probably the most heavy magical realism I've read from him so far. I really enjoy the dual perspective, but I still have so many questions. I doubt (from what I've heard) that they'll be cleared up in the third volume but I'm still intrigued to read the last part! Think I'll take a mini break before doing that though, this stuff is heavy-going...</span>

<div id="review_170362636" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170362636" />
    <a title="Tora" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2109315-tora"><img alt="Tora" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305714464p2/2109315.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/170362636?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tora" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tora" href="/user/show/2109315-tora">Tora</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9788253033808" href="/book/show/11435410-1q84-bok-1-2">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109315-tora?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109315-tora?shelf=japanese">japanese</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109315-tora?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109315-tora?shelf=mannlige-forfattere">mannlige-forfattere</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer170362636" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3223028012551272057">I finished 1Q84 - book 1 & 2 on Monday. Afterwards, I went running in the woods. I ran faster than I have in a while, and my thoughts went back and forth through my head, thinking of everything, anything and nothing at all. It then came to me, I was stuck in that world, Murakami's world. I was scared. I ran through the woods in the middle of the day, and felt scared. Figured the people I met could be anything. Like in Murakami's universe. And I thought that if I'd met a bear, I wouldn't have bee</span>
  <span id="freeText3223028012551272057" style="display:none">I finished 1Q84 - book 1 &amp; 2 on Monday. Afterwards, I went running in the woods. I ran faster than I have in a while, and my thoughts went back and forth through my head, thinking of everything, anything and nothing at all. It then came to me, I was stuck in that world, Murakami's world. I was scared. I ran through the woods in the middle of the day, and felt scared. Figured the people I met could be anything. Like in Murakami's universe. And I thought that if I'd met a bear, I wouldn't have been all that surprised.<br /><br />It took me a while to get into this book, a couple of hundred pages, actually. I was a bit disappointed at first. The simple, straight forward language didn't quite appeal to me this time. I don't think it was any different from his other books, really. I've just read the wrong authors lately. Wrong in the sense of preceding Murakami (I've been spoiled, by my number 1 favorite these days, Tomas Espedal.). And it took me a while to get to know the characters. At first sight, they weren't very Murakami like. They weren't quite the Watanabe character I always long for. But of course they were. I only discovered that after a while. The independent young man is there (as a woman, too this time!), but somehow that is not what the book is about.<br /><br />The story is a strong one, the book a page turner, somewhat similar to Hard-Boiled Wonderland and the End of the World (I loved that one!), only not quite so abstract. It is a heart breaking story, one of broken childhoods, loss, loneliness. It's about love, murder, hope, about strong individuals trying to live their lives their own way. It took me a while to get out of the book as well, to get it out of the system (I'm not sure I have yet). I fell in love with the characters, the universe. 1Q84 is the sad love story from Norwegian Wood and South of the Border, West of the Moon, and it is the abstract world from A Wild Sheep Chase and The Wind-Up Bird Chronicle. And yet, it is completely it's own.<br /><br />As always, I regret finishing the last Murakami book, and envy all of you who haven't yet read it all. Next year, book 3 will be published in Norwegian, and although I do see book 1 &amp; 2 as a complete and finished story, I look forward to it. Of course I do.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3223028012551272057" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12776150093045290965" style="display:none">Murakami, the master weaver of worlds, at his epic best! This is a stunning and complex story expertly woven by alternating the two main characters, Tengo and Aomame. This book defies categorisation. at once drama, thriller, epic and love story it is a literary masterpiece that enthralls the reader from beginning to end. Absolutely the best Murakami, in fact best book I have read for a long long time. Clearly the first two of three books, the end leaves everything hanging and demands you immediately read Book 3. Thank god for the Kindle! ...even though I was on a beach in sub-Saharan Africa I just went online and downloaded Book 3 there and then with Whispernet. <br /><br />A Brilliant literary masterpiece from a modern literary master!</span>

<div id="review_1771205484" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1771205484" />
    <a title="Raquel Baggins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60099374-raquel-baggins"><img alt="Raquel Baggins" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601211766p2/60099374.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1771205484?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Raquel Baggins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Raquel Baggins" href="/user/show/60099374-raquel-baggins">Raquel Baggins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 7503013925764" href="/book/show/30110280-1q84">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60099374-raquel-baggins?shelf=haruki-murakami">haruki-murakami</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60099374-raquel-baggins?shelf=asian-lit">asian-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60099374-raquel-baggins?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1771205484" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4893359892298620762">{Notice: I’ve only read Parts 1 and 2 as the Spanish edition is divided that way and Part 3 is edited as another book}<br/><br/><i>«If you can't understand it without an explanation, you can't understand it with an explanation.»</i><br/><br/>It's the first and only Murakami book that I didn’t like. And I don’t know how to deal with it. I'm confused because he’s <b>always</b> been my favourite author and except for the essay <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2195464.What_I_Talk_About_When_I_Talk_About_Running' title='What I Talk About When I Talk About Running by Haruki Murakami' rel='nofollow noopener'> What I Talk About When I Talk About Running</a>, I've always finished all his books. And I ended up loving th</span>
  <span id="freeText4893359892298620762" style="display:none">{Notice: I’ve only read Parts 1 and 2 as the Spanish edition is divided that way and Part 3 is edited as another book}<br /><br /><i>«If you can't understand it without an explanation, you can't understand it with an explanation.»</i><br /><br />It's the first and only Murakami book that I didn’t like. And I don’t know how to deal with it. I'm confused because he’s <b>always</b> been my favourite author and except for the essay <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2195464.What_I_Talk_About_When_I_Talk_About_Running" title="What I Talk About When I Talk About Running by Haruki Murakami" rel="nofollow noopener"> What I Talk About When I Talk About Running</a>, I've always finished all his books. And I ended up loving the story, the characters, the narrative... Murakami is part of my personality and I wouldn’t be the same without Murakami's books. So this review is probably the one that costs me the most to write in my life. Murakami made me love literature again when I was 16 years old and enjoy again those reading moments before going to sleep, but this book seemed insufferable to me. Well, no, I'm going to clarify a little more: the second part has seemed insufferable to me. I needed answers, that something would happen, I needed to be interested in the novel as I’d been interested in the first part, but no. Nothing of that happened.<br /><br />I loved <b>Aomame</b> from the beginning for being a different character to what I am used to in the works of the Japanese writer, and I liked very much to see represented as a professional killer, a feminist {although she didn’t consider herself as such}, a strong and independent woman and different from the usual female characters of the author. Maybe <b>Tengo</b> is the character we are most used to knowing, and I liked it equally. I liked the fact that the stories were intermingled and that there were such beautiful coincidences building little by little, as only Haruki knows how to build them.<br />But all the things that I liked, I stopped enjoying them in the second part. In the moments of greatest climax, Murakami just cut the whole scene and created a constant anticlimax. The last chapters became very slow and nothing interesting happened that was worthwhile for me to continue reading the book. He hasn’t given answers to most questions posed by the novel, and the conclusion of the parallel worlds didn’t get to hook me at all.<br /><br />It will seem silly, but this book has broken my heart. I don’t think I’m gonna read the third and last part ever {or at least in the next few months}<br /><br />- ESP -<br />{Aviso: solamente he leído los Libros 1 y 2 tal como está editado <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10357575.1Q84" title="1Q84 by Haruki Murakami" rel="nofollow noopener"> 1Q84</a> por Maxi Tusquets}<br /><br /><i>«Conviertes lo que has visto en palabras y lo reconstruyes. De esa forma confirmas tu sitio en el mundo como ser humano.»</i><br /><br />Es el primer y único libro de Murakami que no me ha gustado. Y no sé cómo lidiar con ello. Estoy confusa porque <b>siempre</b> ha sido mi autor favorito y excepto por el ensayo <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7997569.De_qu__hablo_cuando_hablo_de_correr" title="De qué hablo cuando hablo de correr by Haruki Murakami" rel="nofollow noopener"> De qué hablo cuando hablo de correr</a>, siempre he terminado todos sus libros. Y los he terminado amando la historia, los personajes, la narrativa. Murakami forma parte de mi personalidad y yo no sería la misma sin los libros de Murakami. Así que esta reseña es probablemente la reseña que más me cueste escribir en mi vida. Murakami hizo que volviera a amar la literatura cuando tenía 16 años y volver a disfrutar de esos momentos de lectura antes de irme a dormir, pero este libro me ha parecido insufrible. Bueno, no, voy a matizar un poco más: la segunda parte me ha parecido insufrible. Necesitaba respuestas, que pasara algo, que me interesara la novela al igual que me había interesado la primera parte, pero no. No pasó nada de eso.<br /><br />Me encantó el personaje de <b>Aomame</b> desde el principio por ser un personaje diferente a lo que estoy acostumbrada en las obras del escritor japonés, y me gustaba mucho ver representada una asesina a sueldo, feminista {aunque ella no se considerara como tal}, una mujer fuerte e independiente y diferente a los personajes femeninos del autor. Quizás <b>Tengo</b> es el personaje al que más estamos habituados a conocer, y me gustó igualmente. Me gustó el hecho de que las historias se entremezclasen, que hubiera esas coincidencias tan bonitas construyéndose poco a poco, como sólo Haruki sabe construirlas. Pero todas las cosas que me gustaban, dejaron de hacerlo en la segunda parte. En los momentos de mayor clímax de la obra, cortaba de raíz y creaba un anticlímax constante. Los últimos capítulos se me hicieron lentísimos y no ha pasado nada interesante que mereciera la pena para que yo siga leyendo la obra. No ha dado respuestas a la mayoría de preguntas que plantea la novela, y la conclusión de los mundos paralelos no llegó a engancharme.<br /><br />Os parecerá una tontería, pero este libro me ha roto el corazón. No creo que termine la tercera y última parte nunca {o al menos en los próximos meses}.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4893359892298620762" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_211216013" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/211216013" />
    <a title="Alicia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4413327-alicia"><img alt="Alicia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451775923p2/4413327.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/211216013?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alicia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alicia" href="/user/show/4413327-alicia">Alicia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781846554070" href="/book/show/9911160-1q84">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer211216013" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15926993699708000422">Based on the rave reviews, I was very eager to read this book. Many people agreed that the multi-layered plot was brilliant - they couldn't put it down and when they finally finished, the story stayed with them. An amazing story and one that lasts for more than 900 pages? That's every bookworm's dream! A rare gem to be treasured! Unfortunately, I found 1Q84 to be more like a piece of coal - it had the potential to become something beautiful but remained...blah.<br/><br/>For those of you Goodreads-ers who </span>
  <span id="freeText15926993699708000422" style="display:none">Based on the rave reviews, I was very eager to read this book. Many people agreed that the multi-layered plot was brilliant - they couldn't put it down and when they finally finished, the story stayed with them. An amazing story and one that lasts for more than 900 pages? That's every bookworm's dream! A rare gem to be treasured! Unfortunately, I found 1Q84 to be more like a piece of coal - it had the potential to become something beautiful but remained...blah.<br /><br />For those of you Goodreads-ers who read reviews before picking up a book, please take my review with a grain of salt - I am clearly in the minority as most people found this book to be life-changing and you may be one who passionately devours it too. There were certainly parts that I enjoyed, but each time the plot started to build and I thought, "Here it comes - this is what everyone's raving about" and then, nothing. I don't want to spoil the story for you so generally speaking, this is why I gave it one star:<br /><br />1. This book is EXTREMELY repetitive - The same events are explained an unnecessarily excessive amount of times. The repetition does not advance the story in any way; in fact it drags it on. This book (really, books I, II and III) is a good 300 pages too long.<br /><br />2. Dialogue - Characters used words or phrases unnaturally which is likely a translation issue. It was slightly distracting (and yet, endearing) but not a huge issue. What bothered me was parroting - one character would say two sentences and another character would repeat the last sentence as a question. This happened frequently. Also the phrase "so what you're saying is..." was used often and unnecessarily - the character's point was clearly made and didn't require clarification. <br /><br />3. The plot - Oh the plot how you disappoint! There was so much potential here and it didn't go anywhere. There were no twists or turns (events were easily anticipated so I felt deflated when they happened), minimal excitement at most and not in any way compelling. <br /><br />4. The characters - The two main characters' affection for another seemed forced. I don't want to give away too much but the characters evolved in a way that felt like different people edited different sections of the book. <br /><br />5. Breasts, periods and pubic hair - The author writes about all three in detail and often. Generally speaking, I don't have a problem with this at all; however, it didn't feel natural to the characters. I know that sounds weird but it read like a creepy fixation the author had/has vs something the character would focus on.<br /><br />Overall, this book was a terrific disappointment and in desperate need of a capable editor. Should you read this book, I sincerely hope you enjoy it. If you do and you would like to tell me why, I'd love to hear from you because I am confounded by the hype! <br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="15926993699708000422" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_229092376" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/229092376" />
    <a title="Susan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1655341-susan"><img alt="Susan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1237599293p2/1655341.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/229092376?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan" href="/user/show/1655341-susan">Susan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1655341-susan?shelf=novels">novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229092376" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12216593290840659945">1Q84 weighs a couple of pounds and has 944 pages in the hardback edition, but the length and poundage are as nothing compared to its looney gravitational pull. Murakami draws us into a world with two moons, a world that may contain respect but is without overt expressions of love. I suspect that Murakami exerts such a strong pull in the original through his strange prose and use of physical details. Even in English, the style is simple and pictorial, like that of a graphic novel where each actio</span>
  <span id="freeText12216593290840659945" style="display:none">1Q84 weighs a couple of pounds and has 944 pages in the hardback edition, but the length and poundage are as nothing compared to its looney gravitational pull. Murakami draws us into a world with two moons, a world that may contain respect but is without overt expressions of love. I suspect that Murakami exerts such a strong pull in the original through his strange prose and use of physical details. Even in English, the style is simple and pictorial, like that of a graphic novel where each action takes place in a fully realized setting, and the characters are given over to interior monologues and intensely honest conversations.There is always something ominous in 1Q84, where the cultural background is American and European and the characters are Japanese but deeply alienated from society. As in Murakami's other novels, this divergence makes for a fascinating conflict in practically every word. <br /><br />The two main characters, a fitness instructor named Aomame whose name means green pea, and Tengo, a teacher of math and an aspiring novelist, each enter a strange world dominated by a cult and a cadre of "Little People," the latter, beyond good and evil. Once the sinister forces are defeated, the novel transforms itself from an odd fairy tale with helping spirits and boogey men into a conventional love story. Throughout, there are references to Western music, literature, film, and philosophy, and Japanese culture is depicted as fiercely misogynistic and bitterly repressive. This is a daring book packaged, with more filling than necessary, as a fantasy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12216593290840659945" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7147121625628788516">Murakami, I am really sad to say that I am slightly glad to be done with this massive volume! Book 1 and Book 2: done! Book 3 to go! The Japanese writer, Haruki Murakami, is my favorite male writer alive. But, as I said, when I posted about 1Q84 Book 1, I can see flaws in Murakami’s writing even though I am a fan of his work. I also told you that I didn’t want to write a proper review until I finish the book entirely so I still need to read Book 3 before sharing my final thoughts.<br/><br/>Here’s a quick </span>
  <span id="freeText7147121625628788516" style="display:none">Murakami, I am really sad to say that I am slightly glad to be done with this massive volume! Book 1 and Book 2: done! Book 3 to go! The Japanese writer, Haruki Murakami, is my favorite male writer alive. But, as I said, when I posted about 1Q84 Book 1, I can see flaws in Murakami’s writing even though I am a fan of his work. I also told you that I didn’t want to write a proper review until I finish the book entirely so I still need to read Book 3 before sharing my final thoughts.<br /><br />Here’s a quick summary of what I gathered throughout these 800 pages: We’re in Tokyo, in 1Q84 (yes, this is a dystopian novel!) and a lot is happening during the fictionalized year of 1984 (Hi, Orwell 🙌)The plot follows the lives of two characters: Tengo and Aomame. Initially, they have nothing in common but, during Book 2, their storylines come together. After a long and strong story that explores abuse, punishment and redemption, the characters notice a second moon which reminds them of the alternate reality in which they’re living.<br /><br />Although I find the whole concept incredibly interesting I couldn’t stand Tengo and his pedophilic behaviour. I thought 'Maybe in Book 2 it won’t be just as bad'. <br /><br />For more reviews, follow me on Instagram @booksturnyouon.</span>

<div id="review_679663307" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/679663307" />
    <a title="Khris Sellin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2327871-khris-sellin"><img alt="Khris Sellin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592316004p2/2327871.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/679663307?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khris Sellin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khris Sellin" href="/user/show/2327871-khris-sellin">Khris Sellin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer679663307" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1045256194336693800">I'm not sure where to begin with this review. HUGE disappointment. And that's an understatement. The biggest mystery is how/why I actually read all 925 painful pages.<br/><br/>The story is set in 1984 (but yet sometimes in 1Q84 - not even worth explaining) in Tokyo. I guess the backdrop to it all is that, 20 years earlier, at 10 years old, Tengo and Aomame were schoolmates and they fell in love without ever actually speaking to each other. And circumstances beyond their control separate them soon after an</span>
  <span id="freeText1045256194336693800" style="display:none">I'm not sure where to begin with this review. HUGE disappointment. And that's an understatement. The biggest mystery is how/why I actually read all 925 painful pages.<br /><br />The story is set in 1984 (but yet sometimes in 1Q84 - not even worth explaining) in Tokyo. I guess the backdrop to it all is that, 20 years earlier, at 10 years old, Tengo and Aomame were schoolmates and they fell in love without ever actually speaking to each other. And circumstances beyond their control separate them soon after and they haven't seen each other since, but they haven't stopped thinking about each other in all these years. OK, I can get on board with that. I'm a hopeless romantic. "If you can love someone with your whole heart, even one person, then there's salvation in life. Even if you can't get together with that person." <br /><br />In their adult lives, Tengo is an aspiring writer who also teaches math at a local "cram" school; Aomame (the translation of her name is "green peas" - cute, isn't it?) is a trainer at a sports club, but she also has a side job as an assassin for "the Dowager," a rich older woman who dispatches Aomame to kill only those who deserve it - men who have abused women in some way. The Dowager also runs a safe house for battered women. <br /><br />There's also a fantastical story going on here, about a religious cult. One of its young members, Eriko Fukada ("Fuka-Eri"), escaped at 10 years old and has been living with a family friend ever since. She's now 17 and has written an amazing story, one that was edited and rewritten (unbeknownst to the public) by Tengo, and it becomes a huge bestseller. It's all about Little People, who jump out of a dead goat's mouth, and they say "Ho-ho" a lot, and apparently they wield a lot of power. But is this just a story or is she recounting what really happened back at that cult?? The plot thickens...<br /><br />So I don't know if things get "Lost in Translation," but the dialogue/narration is ludicrous. OK, Fuka-Eri is supposed to speak in a stilted, monotone fashion, asking questions with no question marks, but everyone else has these completely ridiculous, nonrealistic conversations, and it was really frustrating to read through that nonsense, especially from an author who is so highly regarded. <br /><br />Then there is the gratuitous sex and pedophilia. Listen, I'm no prude, but the characters' obsession with sex was also bordering on ludicrous. And their fascination with their own bodies and sexual organs. <br /><br />THEN there is the needless repetition and the author's insistence on pounding us all over the head with explanations:<br />"I'm a Perceiver, and you're a Receiver."<br />"In other words, you 'perceive' things and I 'receive' them?"<br />Duh, ok.<br /><br />SPOILER ALERT: In 1Q84 (but not 1984), there are two moons in the sky! And the people who see the two moons get REALLY freaked out about this. Each one notices the two moons, then we get to read for 15 pages about how they're getting totally freaked out about the TWO MOONS! Then the next character discovers that there are TWO MOONS in the sky!! 15 more pages about them freaking out. What's the significance of the two $#%*&amp; moons in the sky??? Who the *&amp;$% knows!!! (And, frankly, who cares)<br /><br />Also, there's another character, Ushikawa, who works for the religious group as a sort of spy. He's apparently not very attractive. He has a misshapen head and short bandy legs. We get this description of him at least 20 times. I'm not exaggerating. Maybe because the book is 925 freaking pages, the author thinks we might have forgotten Ushikawa and his misshapen head. If only we could be so lucky...<br /><br />I think I held on because, as I said above, I'm a sucker for a cheesy love story, and I just wanted these crazy kids to get together. But admittedly, through all the glop, I got sucked into the other story line as well and wanted to see what would happen. Big fizzle. (Remember how we all got sucked into the TV show "Lost" and then the big finale - What the what??? Like that, except with bad dialogue) Characters and plot lines are introduced, only to disappear in one way or another without any real explanation or resolution.<br /><br />And to sum up my point about ludicrous dialogue/narration and obsession with sex and body parts, here is Aomame's thought process toward the end of the book. Oh, another spoiler alert. She has some friends who died in the past. Not really a spoiler. OK, here's the quote:<br />"Aomame mourned the deaths of these two friends deeply. It saddened her to think that these women were forever gone from the world. And she mourned their lovely breasts - breasts that had vanished without a trace." <br />Yes, I think we can all agree, when we're reflecting on the loss of our loved ones, we bemoan the loss of their breasts, and their penises - not to mention those great asses - that we'll never ever see again, that have, in a word, VANISHED!<br /><br />Sweet love story, though.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1045256194336693800" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="James" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6022914-james"><img alt="James" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421168922p2/6022914.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/529134030?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer529134030" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15440961689089415136">This is a strange review as I've only read book one so far.<br/><br/>1Q84 Book One was our work book club choice this month as we assumed it was the first in a three book series, but having read to the end of book one it just stops dead. No real build up, no reveal, no twist. Just stops dead. Clearly we now realise that books one and two are actually two volumes in a single novel. They should probably be read back-to-back rather than reading book one now and book two later (probably next year for me now).</span>
  <span id="freeText15440961689089415136" style="display:none">This is a strange review as I've only read book one so far.<br /><br />1Q84 Book One was our work book club choice this month as we assumed it was the first in a three book series, but having read to the end of book one it just stops dead. No real build up, no reveal, no twist. Just stops dead. Clearly we now realise that books one and two are actually two volumes in a single novel. They should probably be read back-to-back rather than reading book one now and book two later (probably next year for me now).<br /><br />Consequently, it's hard to rate it. I have absolutely no idea where this book is going, or even much idea what's going on. And that's to be expected now I know I haven't read the whole book. I'm going to say I liked it, but I'm not <i>really</i> liking it and I don't think it's awesome. Yet. I reserve the right to change this when I get to book two later on. (Book three is a whole different topic, that does appear to be designed to be read as a separate - sequel - book.)<br /><br />It's a very interesting novel though. Alternating between two viewpoint characters of Aomame (not to be confused with edamame) - a fitness instructor <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[with a sideline in assassinating abusive men <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> who climbs down an access stairway from a freeway to find herself in an alternate 1984, which she terms 1Q84 - and Tengo - a maths teacher who wants to be an author who ends up rewriting a novel by a young girl for a literary competition. Both characters find themselves drawn into an increasingly strange alternate reality.<br /><br />Along the way, we are introduced to a women's refuge that resolves abuse in a somewhat final way, a farming community that has become a religious cult, a dyslexic seventeen year old girl who has written a potentially prize-winning story, an editor and a professor who both have their own reasons to have the story win the prize, and a slow reveal of the connections between nearly all the characters.<br /><br />On the downsides, the book has a couple of obsessions. Murakami seems overly keen to describe the breasts of almost all the main (female) characters in the novel (often repeatedly) - Aomame's are too small, Ayumi's are larger, and Fuka-Eri's are perfect (well she is seventeen) and look great in a sweater. I was glad he drew the line at describing the Dowager's. Coupled with Aomame's obsession with having sex with balding middle-aged men (Sean Connery is her ideal) with the 'right-shaped' head, it starts to feel a little like Murakami is trying to slip his own fantasies into an otherwise fascinating story...</span>
  <a data-text-id="15440961689089415136" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_867080788" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/867080788" />
    <a title="Kaitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin"><img alt="Kaitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481663259p2/19126246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/867080788?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781846554070" href="/book/show/9911160-1q84">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer867080788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14762224585032039178">This is a highly interesting story in all sense of the word and I cannot think how to begin to describe all of the feelings I encountered whilst reading this. This was my first Murakami read and I have to confess I knew next to nothing about it, or him, or George Orwell's 1984 which is referenced a lot in this novel, however despite these challenges I did end up really enjoying the entire two books and I will certainly be picking up book 3 when I can to find out how it all draws to a close.<br/><br/>The s</span>
  <span id="freeText14762224585032039178" style="display:none">This is a highly interesting story in all sense of the word and I cannot think how to begin to describe all of the feelings I encountered whilst reading this. This was my first Murakami read and I have to confess I knew next to nothing about it, or him, or George Orwell's 1984 which is referenced a lot in this novel, however despite these challenges I did end up really enjoying the entire two books and I will certainly be picking up book 3 when I can to find out how it all draws to a close.<br /><br />The story itself is hard to describe, being told from two points of view, Aomame and Tengo. These two characters are integral to the plot and they are both so meticulously detailed and scrutanising in the way that they view the world that reading through their eyes is a very strange experience and truly brings you into their new world in an entirely different way.<br /><br />Tengo is a writer of fiction who is struggling to find his own vision and create a masterwork to give him a 'name' in the literary world. He has a passion for Mathematics and teaches at a local school during the week. He enjoys the company of older women, finding no love for those who are of his age or younger, and taking solace in the time he spends with his older, married girlfriend each week. He is a careful character and doesn't like to get involved in anything he doesn't see as morally right or unsuspicious. However the story he is a part of makes these decisions hard for him, and he crosses some lines that he may not normally have done so...<br /><br />Aomame is a highly trained muscle therapist and she has become rather renowned for her skills in the trade. She is a lonely individual who has few friends and little time for fun, more contemplation. Her style and sexual partners are very much constant throughout the text, however she does have a longing for someone else who always seems to be out of her grasp. Working as a muscle therapist is but one of her jobs, the other being of a far more sensitive matter. She helps to make the world better, or so she tries to convince herself...<br /><br />Fuka-Eri is another key character from the story although we don't actually see from her point of view. She is a cryptic character and throughout the entire novel she seems to know far more than she lets on or that she is able to confess to the main characters. She is a very capable, bright and knowledgeable character and although she lacks certain skills she is able to come across as a pivotal person in the novel.<br /><br />Overall one of the aspects I truly enjoyed was the writing which is on a whole new, mystical level from most other books I have read. Murakami is clearly very talented and even when I truly couldn't grasp how everything would come together at all, I found that I loved the writing and character development enough to keep being sucked back into the world without question. <br /><br />I also loved the character development, much of which is illustrated through the thoughts and contemplation of the two main characters who are, in their own way, critical, analytic, and clever. Their perception of the world of 1Q84 makes it all the more enthralling to read about and all the more magical and captivating to be a part of as you read. The style of narration was truly ensnaring and I loved that element. <br /><br />There is a mystical and fantastical element to the world which I didn't know was a part of the novel but I did absolutely love it as this is what I love in books and the adult writing brought a much more complex tone to the magic and made it hard to define or interpret, yet still exciting enough to encaptured my thoughts.<br /><br />On the whole I would say that if you enjoy adult writing, mystical and magical ideas, well-crafted plot and a superb style of storytelling then this is a brilliant read, the only reason that I took off a star is that the ending leaves much open, and I hope that when I read book 3 these questions raised by the ending will be answered and I will be able to grant book 3 a 5* rating instead of 4*s</span>
  <a data-text-id="14762224585032039178" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <span id="freeText11589523989502109083" style="display:none">Help, I have fallen down a rabbit hole and there’s no way out. <br />Never have I ever been so confused, yet so intrigued. I am feeling so many emotions all at once, directed at the characters but mostly at Murakami for fucking with my feelings like this. If **** and ****** don’t get together at the end of this that’s very Murakami but also, NO I CAN’T ACCEPT IT I AM SO SAD, WHY DOES HE ALWAYS DO THIS? It’s so ... poetic? So absurd and mystical and so well-written and mmm the similarities and threads that all connect through the two different perspectives 💅🏻 That’s taste. If literature was food Murakami would be a gourmet dish. He’d be a Michelin star restaurant. He’d be enchilladas drenched in salsa. ❤️ (If you can’t tell, I just finished this book, it’s very late and I am still coming down from a Murakami-high.) I appreciate the references to 1984 by George Orwell because that book is god-tier literature.<br />The third book will surely finish the second one’s job and murder me with an icepick to my neck, green pea-style. Makes no sense if you’re not a whore for Murakami like I am. Oh well, we can’t all be me.</span>
